Offer a peach in return for jade,
All comes from the Creator, who knows repayment.

**To Judge of the Shanglin Prefecture, in the Style of Cao E**

Without your command, the characters were not complete,
Yet in my sleeve, I knew them from crossing great rivers.
Village songs and roadside chants linger like swift horses,
The two sweet pear trees recall the renowned worthy.
Ten marvels of the precious hall—

**Golden Turtle Peak**
Once it bore the square Penglai from the sea,
Here it coils, never to return.
A thousand years have divined its divine splendor,
Ashamed I lack the eight-pillar talent to hold up the sky.

**Literary Brush Peak**
Its solitary crest soars into the vast, empty void,
Its distant form seems to pierce the heavens like a bookshelf.
This land has long produced officials and scholars,
The earth’s vital qi breeds literary heroes.

**Greedy Wolf Peak**
Among the seven stars of the Dipper, it shines with literary brilliance,
How did this mountain rise so tall from the earth?
I long to soar to its highest summit,
To forever join the earth’s tongue in aiding peace.

**Lotus Peak**
Jade-like flowers display their artistry, distant and graceful,
The Buddha’s hair emits a subtle fragrance, drifting into the mysterious.
If only a heavenly wind could carry a single leaf,
It too would drift eastward with Taiyi.

**Square Rock Peak**
A stone fan opens into the empty sky,
Its scenery surpasses Penglai.
At times, when the azure heavens descend to pay homage,
The wind’s axle briefly rests on green moss.

**White Deer Peak**
How many years have passed since the white deer came?
The perilous peak still leans against the blue sky.
In leisure, not only do I discuss true secrets,
I also seek a forest monk to ask about Chan.

**Ancient City Peak**
Layered summits, emerald hues shrouded in verdure,
The ancient ramparts have no foundation, yet the gaze never ends.
At midnight, under the bright moon, the heavens’ music resounds,
I suspect a crane has returned from the distant east.

**Flying Tumbleweed Peak**
A tumbleweed flies from the sea,
Cinnabar cliffs and emerald walls stand tall in the distance.
Where now is the immortal who played the sheng?
Only peach trees, a thousand in bloom, remain.

**Purple Terrace Peak**
The terrace peak juts out east of the Yue River,
A winding path of black and purple threads through the verdant hues.
How many times has the bright moon seen immortals descend?
Their coral pendants tinkle in the celestial wind.

**Great Peace Peak**
The benevolent winds of a bright age spread great peace,
How fortunate this mountain is to bear such a fine name.
Several times I have climbed to its summit to gaze,
The six directions stretch boundlessly, heaven and earth clear.

**Eight Poems on True Immortals**

**Palace of the Turtle Peak Immortal**
From the sea, the peak surges forth like a golden turtle,
A dark palace stands, firmly constructed.

**The Eternal Heroic Spirit**
The heroic spirit never fades,
Its earthly station lofty and pure.
By moonlight, the cinnabar well lies deep;
In spring winds, the green peach blossoms bloom.
A single loyalty upholds the realm,
A crimson edict bestows honor and praise.

**Dragon Pool Flying Waterfall**
A thousand-foot dragon’s maw—no ladder may scale,
A flying torrent plunges straight down in rainbow spray.
The immortals, late returning from gathering essences,
Idly play with murmuring streams and medicinal mud.

**Bamboo Cliff After Snow**
The sacred cliff retains its auspicious snow,
Dawn’s light now brightens the clearing sky.
Piled whiteness cradles the first rays,
Frozen splendor gleams in the Great Clarity.
Low, it buries the bent bamboo;
High, it crushes the ancient pine.
I long to soar to the perilous summit,
Strolling at leisure in a crane-feather cloak.

**Immortal Isle’s Sacred Fungus**
Dazzling, resplendent—threefold blossoms flourish,
The harmonious qi of the Great Peace nurtures this spiritual root.
Dwelling hidden here, how to repay its grace?
Plucked and offered to Yu Yan, presented to the Supreme Lord.

**Returning Tide at Green Bank**
At the farthest bank, the cold tide recedes,
Winding and distant, the view stretches wide.
Grass roots cling to scattered stones,
The river’s mouth reveals level sands.
Birds peck at the broken green mud,
Boats moor to ancient, slanting willows.
In but a moment, the tide returns again—
From here, I set sail on a transcendent raft.

**Travelers at South Pond**
Wheels and hooves rush to and fro,
The road links north and south, passing through Min’s mountains.
Pity the restless souls in the red dust—
How can they compare to the immortal palace’s leisurely days and months?

**Wood Ridge’s Woodcutter’s Song**
The woodcutter’s song echoes from Wood Ridge,
The rugged path darkens as the sun sinks.
Melodious, it drifts across winding streams,
Gentle, it emerges from layered forests.
Low, it mingles with the golden cicadas’ tune;
High, it follows the white cranes’ cries.
Within the jade palace, no vulgar notes—
Hearing this, the heart’s cares dissolve.

**Bell Mountain’s Pagoda**
As the sun rises, Bell Mountain’s air feels new,
A seven-tiered pagoda surges in phosphorescent splendor.
Since ancient times, this blessed land has borne the wise and noble—
In this sagely age, those inscribed are not few.

**Two Poems for Xu Nancun**
Mud and wood assume forms—how laughable indeed,
Yet you patch rustic words into poetic lines.
Sir, you are no Master Pang,
Yet how does your lamp’s light pervade the great chiliocosm?

Ashamed I lack the skill to season the broth,
I playfully blend all things into fragrant harmony.
Feasting in the butcher’s hall, one knows many flavors—
Mock not the mountain dweller’s wild greens and amaranth.

**Ten Marvelous Peaks of Jade Mountain**

**Golden Immortal Peak**
The cinnabar turtle’s thousand-year embers have turned to ash,
Only its towering stone halls remain, jagged and grand.
Casually ascend the summit to gaze afar—
Beyond the clouds, the verdant Five Terraces rise.

**Heavenly Pillar Peak**
Step by step, nearing the mountain’s front,
Suddenly, bell tones shatter the dawn mist.
A peak abruptly rises, sheer as a wall—
Its strength seems enough to prop up the sky.

**Sunrise Peak**
At dawn, the stone cliff pierces the clouds,
Dripping spring sounds chill the night air.
I thought only the gibbons’ cries marked the predawn,
Yet when I open the door, the sun has climbed three poles high.

**Third Young Master’s Peak**
By the Fishing Creek, a fishing boat,
I ask the passerby—do you know his surname?
With a smile, I point to this mountain’s refined charm:
Wildflowers, singing birds—enough for carefree wandering.

**Golden Splendor Peak**
From afar, it seems a painting, seizing heaven’s artistry,
Hazy mountain light reflects the evening glow.
The pines and firs atop the ridge hold ancient intent—
Who knows that in the dead of night, the robe has already been passed?

**Rising Cloud Peak**
For miles, the path winds around the mountain’s flank,
Dawn’s hues remain dim, the mist not yet dispersed.
Scratching my head in the blue haze, I lose the way—
Only the sound of a single thunderclap from the mountain’s base.

**Treasure Terrace Peak**
Layer upon layer, its form rivals Kunlun’s cliffs,
The gallery path seems celestial, beyond climbing.
A single point of pure light ever shines before me—
Pine winds and cassia moons make a fine livelihood.

**Great Seat Peak**
After rain, the mountain mist dyes the peaks dark,
The stone path is slick, few travelers pass.
The meditator naturally grasps the dharma of meditation—
From where does the cold bell toll at dawn?

**Jade Angelica Peak**
A single heavenly flower, still unopened,
Who plucks it and does not offer it?
Straight to the summit’s peak I sit,
At times, its fragrance wafts to Tiantai.

**Twin Lads Peak**
The hanging terrace’s bright mirror turns with the clear light,
The Jade Maiden once tested the morning’s zither.
Ever like maidens in their youthful days,
Forever young, their hair never turns white.

**East Stream**
The stream’s voice is just this—water murmuring,
Ever constricted, it flows away and does not return.
Countless worldly affairs are all thus—
How can they compare to the white gulls’ leisure on the sand?

**West Stream**
In the mountains, idle guests visit one another,
I ask those coming from the west—their intent?
Neither increasing nor decreasing, without hindrance,
Following the current, they pass through the Heavenly River.

**Jade Cliff**
I love the mountain, thus I love the jagged stone,
The jade-grade mountain becomes a jade brother.
Twin streams divide, sending white egrets forth,
Ten peaks encircle, half green and half withered.
In the mortar of light clouds, tea holds many flavors;
By the lamp of the waning moon, a volume of scripture.
By chance, I reach the upper hall to ask of Chan—
Surely they know I am no ordinary man.

**Two Poems Seeing Off Chen Daoxing to Dragon-Tiger Mountain**
Within Zhongnan Mountain lie many fine scenes,
Yet alas, the ambition for fame and rank still smolders.
On the Dragon-Tiger Board, a new name appears—
Plum blossoms first claim the hundred flowers’ primacy.

Recommending the true and evaluating the worthy—this is ancient numen,
Aiding others’ good deeds paves the way ahead.
Magpies call to report news of peace—
I compose these verses to send you on your journey.

**Matching Monk Dejian of White Cloud**
Speak not of Qin, Sui, Jin, Han, or Tang—
The three gates, the thatched hut, the land of white clouds.
The water buffalo does not leave; the mountain’s old man is false—
I ask you: in those years, did you burn incense?

**Four Occasional Poems**
Within stillness, heaven and earth reckon not the spring,
Affirming and negating—let the myriad things whirl.
Where now are Xing Yuan and Zui Bai?
Beyond the clouds, green mountains—mountains beyond clouds.

I once heard the song of the captured unicorn,
Only to learn that Master Gao was a fine man.
The lotus flower, about to speak, holds many sentiments—
How can it compare to the speechless flower’s sunlit spring?

Where to seek the bright moon and clear wind?
Poets’ bitter thoughts dissolve in wine.
Forgetting schemes, unconcerned if others understand,
The sand gulls alone know this heart.

Two autumns have passed since I forgot you,
This feeling remains unspoken—do you know it?
Beyond the green mountain gate, many sentiments linger,
Left for poets to take as their topic.

*End of Xu Xian’s Literary Works, Scroll Seven*
*Beginning of Xu Xian’s Literary Works, Scroll Eight*

**Lyrics**

*"To the Tune of ‘Linjiang Xian’ – The Hall of Kindred Harmony"*
Painting, calligraphy, zither, and chess—joys of life,
A household brimming with harmony, round as the moon.
Grandchildren in festive play fill the hall,
Together we pour a cup of wine,
As one we toast to boundless years.

Mind fixed on transcribing the *Huangting* script’s secrets,
Within the sprouting bud, the cinnabar field is nurtured.
Wealth and honor, like the immortals’ greens—all are but the Dao.
Names inscribed in golden registers,
Sleeves brushed by the incense of the imperial censer.

*"To the Tune of ‘Qianqiu Sui’ – The Hall of Swallowing Joy"*
Turtle Peak’s blessed land,
Mountains and waters rich with wonders.
Remember the old prophecy of the net’s catch—
Heaven-sown unicorns,
Phoenixes and mandarin ducks, omens among men.

And now, behold!
A son’s ambition fulfilled, the bow set aside,
Young, he ascends the ranks of scholars.
Still more joy—both parents live,
Long may we wish them,
A thousand, thousand years.

Lao Lai in motley play,
The Queen Mother’s feast at Jasper Pool,
Together we revel,
The hall filled with laughter,
Golden goblets drunk with mirth.

*"To the Tune of ‘Xiangsi Yin’ – For Elder Shen Jian"*
The spirit of mountains and peaks stirs jade’s essence,
Rising to form Turtle Peak.
Clear mountains, graceful waters,
Fortune comes in fleeting delight.
Should one ask of future affairs and profit,
But store up hidden virtue within the square inch of the heart.
Plant the locust tree, as the prophecy foretells—
Surely it will make you one of the Three Dukes.

*"To the Tune of ‘Qingping Le’ – For Zhou Tong"*
Seated in the hall’s purity and elegance,
With joy, hand in hand.

The moon clears, the wind gentle—such grace is found everywhere,
Best to chant poems and pour wine.
Autumn comes, cold dew chills,
Yet why not paint lightly or boldly as you please?
By the fence, golden chrysanthemums bloom,
Their late virtue still fragrant as they age.

*"To the Tune of ‘Geng Lou Zi’ – For Zhou Ming"*
A tranquil family’s virtue is finest,
Delighting in pond lotuses and window grasses.
Leaning on the desk, resting by the rail,
All pure fragrance flows as one.
A sliver of moon hangs low,
Unnoticed, the fifth watch arrives.
The lamp reports joy as magpies call,
Morning dawns bright and clear.

*"To the Tune of ‘Huan Xi Sha’ – For Lin Zhuang"*
Right and wrong fill the world’s questions,
Better to learn the Dao and refine the elixir of immortals,
Still whistling long as you enter the deep mountains.
Three paths grow wild—who will tend them?
Chrysanthemums and pines as friends, the gate of glory barred,
Find peace in seclusion where white clouds idle.

*"To the Tune of ‘Xiang Jian Ju’ – For Zhang Guilong"*
Wind mild, sun warm—two or three springs,
Rain clears, skies blush red and purple.
A hundred flowers like brocade, willows like silk floss,
From the high tower, pearl curtains roll up.
The master’s home,
Once more welcomes the returning pair of swallows,
Let the calendar be woven anew.

*"To the Tune of ‘Ye Jin Men’ (Also ‘Xi Xiang Yi Qiao’) – For Guo Yongfang"*
Clouds thin, rain thick,
February’s hundred flowers bloom red.
Travelers come and go,
East or west, as the wind differs for ox and horse.
Mountains green again,
Waters green again,
The path winds nine turns like a sheep’s gut.
Best to entrust your heart’s affairs to the messenger,
For five times five marks the future’s course.

*"To the Tune of ‘Ying Tian Chang’ – For Zheng Ruxian"*
Swallows and orioles dance face to face,
Relying on the Eastern Lord to rule forever.
Rain then clear, clear then rain,
Playfully ask the peach blossoms—they smile but do not speak.
The sun sets behind western hills,
Clouds veil the dusk,
Crows weary of flight return home.
Should you ask where the future’s goodness lies,
In the full moon of the fifteenth night.

*"To the Tune of ‘Shan Hua Zi’ – For Guo Yili of Tianyi Temple"*
Alone he bolts the wicker gate, unconcerned with worldly affairs,
What in this world equals clouds’ idleness?
Do not say the heartless always drift from the peaks,
For even they know to return—not as mist, not as smoke.
In nothingness, King Xiang’s dream of Wu,
Cold in brocade robes.
One offering of heart’s incense,
This is the true dwelling in famous mountains.

*"To the Tune of ‘Shuang Tian Xiao Jiao’ – For Taihe Mountain Monk De Run"*
A staff flies through empty space,
A hundred-foot robe and bowl passed down.
Silently listening to morning bells and evening drums,
Fire extinguished in the heart’s core.
Incense fills the golden censer,
Seated atop the high peak.
Should one ask of Śākyamuni’s heir,
What is the cave of *ā-luó*?

*"To the Tune of ‘Dian Jiang Chun’ – For Shijing of Yueshan Temple"*
A karmic bond for this generation,
The school of learning flourishes, the Dharma treasure’s sound rings clear.
True and not false from the start,
At the critical moment, the patriarch returns.
I once sought the false,
But now, at the sound of the bell, I strike,
Laying down the hammer and tongs.

*"To the Tune of ‘Yu Lou Chun’"*
All contention over purity is but the Buddha’s law,
Tending life among the flower-and-herb railings.
The old master of Yunmen startles all,
Best to question and answer with the *huatou*.
This karmic bond is a seamless pagoda,
Return to me with Deshan’s shout and blow.
From here to the Western Heaven, ten thousand miles and more,
Walking to and fro, again and again.

*"Repairing the Palace, Sewing Robes – To the Tune of ‘Man Gong Chun’"*
Mending the eastern wall, patching the western,
Every task uneven, not the same.
Where the human heart is steadfast, stone can be pierced,
Let us all exert our strength together.
Embroidered silk robes,
Stitched silk skirts,
Costing a thousand needles, ten thousand threads.
Where effort is great, value is high,
Surely fame will rise and shine.

*"To the Tune of ‘Xi Qian Ying’"*
Seeing no shadow, hearing no sound,
Yet in the dark room, a spirit lingers.
Not incense by morning, not lamp by night,
Sincerity may dwell in the square inch of the heart.
Turning to clouds, covering as rain,
Worldly affairs cycle thus.
Ancient vines and old trees endure through many springs,
Now once more renewed.

*"To the Tune of ‘Xi Xi Sha’ – For Painter Cai"*
A master of brush and ink, the world acclaims,
I once composed verses for *Huatang Chun*,
Who knew the marvel would capture the spirit?
Four limbs flawless in beauty,
Eyes left unmarked to preserve truth,
Was Gu Kaizhi ever truly a fool?

*"To the Tune of ‘Huatang Chun’"*
Clear wind and bright moon cost no coin,
The brush’s *qi* and charm are natural.
Loosening robes, squatting on bricks—called a true immortal,
This too is a chance encounter.
Depicting gods, ghosts, and a hundred strange things,
With thick smoke and pale ink, fresh and vivid,
Everyone says it rivals my own skill.

*"To the Tune of ‘Shang Ping Xi’ – For a Young Man of Changyi Bound for Hunan"*
Good child,
With aspirations for the four directions.

**"To the Tune of ‘Pu Sa Man’ – For Guo Dongtang of Tianwang, Bound for Tongcheng"**
A true man’s heart rides a white steed,
By chance beneath blossoms with his beloved,
Exchanging words, baring their hearts,
Wine cups filled once more.
Where lies longing? For her lover,
She straightens his lapels again.
A song in her heart, a handkerchief in hand,
A flute beneath the pillow, a lute in its bag—
Rising, she sings in the Yue mode.
Silken bed-words urge her lord:
*"You must learn from Su Qin,
That good fortune aligns with desire,
To gird a seal and bear gold."*

**"To the Tune of ‘Pu Sa Man’ – For Tongcheng"**
Tongcheng has its own Lu Shu,
Where he dons robes, holds his alms bowl,
And cultivates the Way.
Suddenly awakened, he asks of the path ahead—
The road ahead lies smooth and level.
*"Do not shrink from a thousand miles’ distance,
But vow the bodhi resolve.
When good deeds joyfully complete,
A true man shall bear witness."*

**"To the Tune of ‘Gui Zi Yao’ – Exhorting Painter Cai"**
Have you not seen
The immortals of Penglai’s three isles,
Alone reigning amid clouds,
Their palaces of lapis lazuli revealed?
Beyond the fence-gate, white as silk,
For rough sketches—take care,
Lest dust ever soil them.

**"For Tai Linjun on Asking Matters – To the Tune of ‘Xi Jiang Yue’"**
They speak of the Layman of Xiangcheng,
And call Jia Dao a transcendent talent.
With ladders and go-betweens for literary ascent,
All rests on merit and fame.
*"Snatching mustard seeds"*—his descendants’ fortune,
Did he not know of the Wangs’ three sophoras?
The third son was indeed the third top graduate,
His name eternal through the ages.

**"For the Dragon Boat Craftsman – To the Tune of ‘Xi Jiang Yue’"**
Knowing the art of grasping dragons,
Daring to present a bow’s design.
On the Mid-Autumn moonlit night, reaching the Milky Way,
All on earth gaze up at me.
Crafting a thousand-year reputation,
Together they praise a generation’s elegance.
A silk banner bestowed as a gift,
Better than a pig’s trotter or a cup of wine.

**"Love-Matching Poem"**
Silken breezes in the third month’s festival,
A heart adrift in fragrance.
Hard to restrain—the stirring of youthful passion,
Why not let it burst forth?
Following the beat, tuning the tongue,
Never waste spring’s light.
All sixty-six—mere romantic dalliances,
Amid the flower-market’s throng.
Since you stand in the highest vantage to admire blossoms,
No need to feign reluctance at the door.

**"For the Prefect of Min County"**
A stellar envoy, a paragon among hosts,
The brush-tip governor of the Seven Min.

**On the Transformations of Nature and the Seasons**

In years past, when Shao was established in Jian,
The elders rejoiced to cling and detain him.
Truly, his governance was as clear as water,
Beneath the sweet pear’s shade, clouds drifted.
Again, word came of virtuous rule in the south,
The lanes sang his praise, the roads hummed his name.
Now, blossoms fill the county—
Prefect Pan cherishes them,
Yet need not cling so tightly.

**My Own Pleasure in Travel**

Amid the marketplace’s revelry,
I hear the post station’s wind and moon make fine scenes.
I ask in jest—
Is it true there are brocade embankments by the thousand,
And his reputation resounds through the imperial capital?

**On Secretary Tingyu of Tailin’s Inquiry**

Before and after this life—unfathomable,
Why not shave my head and learn from the Tathāgata?
Where is the Tathāgata?
Bound for Tiantai.
The summit of Great Emaciation Ridge remains untouched,
Why sweep the dust from the mirror stand?
For now, ascend the highest peak and sit,
And make this my livelihood.

**For Five Colleagues**

I hear the river village was snow-laden last night,
And now the plum blossoms gleam white.
The southern branch bears tidings of spring’s arrival—
Snow and plum blossoms open side by side,
What fine spirits they evoke.

Plucking plum blossoms before the snow, wordless,
Plum and snow truly like a painting,
Enhanced by moonlight gracing the pavilions.
The mood of plum, snow, and moon—hard to fathom,
With two or three cups.

*From Xu Xian’s "Rhapsodies on Elegance," Scroll Eight*

**Petition for the Appointment of Xuanbiao Zhenjun**

We humbly submit: though the Gate of Heaven stands but a footstep away, none have prostrated in loyal remonstrance. The sacred precincts are stern and bright—how dare we presume to petition before the celestial throne? Overwhelmed and trembling, we can neither advance nor retreat.

Your servant [Name] respectfully reflects: the Primordial Master, the Heavenly Master, holds the sacred rank, his Dao transmitted from the Prior Heaven, his teachings proclaimed through a hundred generations as the covenant of truth, an eternal transmission for the unlearned. We, your servant, though charged with ritual duties and bound by precepts, dare not act alone in private schemes without first submitting this plea. There are established precedents—we must await the guidance of left and right hands, never straying from the law. The ranks of East and West must stand as one, each in their proper place. On an auspicious day, we shall perform the Luotian Jiao rites to express our gratitude to Lingji Zhenren. Yet we fear that fellow altar practitioners may not yet heed the wondrous teachings, and though we strive together in the Dao, we dare not prolong this petition further. The statutes prescribe penalties for transgressions—we tremble lest we violate their severity.

**Petition of Gratitude for the Appointment of Xuanbiao Zhenjun**

We, in awe and trepidation, bow our heads again and again. We reverently consider the Marshal, the Great Dharma Master, whose merit pervades transformation and nurture, whose Dao penetrates the profound and subtle. As rivers and marshes flow boundlessly, all return to the sea in homage. Yet before the radiance of sun and moon, who would dare cover their eyes? We gaze toward Heaven to repay its grace, yet our devotion remains imperfect, our efforts exhausted. Our transgressions pile like mountains, our merits weigh no more than dust. Yet by your gracious indulgence, you heed our words without rejection.

We, your servant, though dwelling in the Cavern of Truth, remain unenlightened, aged and incapable. Yet through the intercession of memorials, we are deemed worthy. How could we presume to advance in the immortal ranks, coveting merit or usurping rank? Now, as Xu [Name] and others are elevated in rank and bestowed imperial favor, we, who partake of the land’s bounty, share in the gratitude for life’s blessings. With hands raised and feet dancing, we unite in reverent joy. To speak further would be presumptuous—we fear only transgression.

**Petition of Gratitude for the Bestowal of Rank**

The rites for warding off calamity and averting disaster are solemnly observed. Those who build merit and accumulate virtue deserve advancement in the immortal ranks. Though the divine cannot be measured, our thoughts and words must be laid before them.

We, in awe and trepidation, bow our heads again and again. We recall the Yellow Emperor, who sought the essence of the supreme Dao from Guangchengzi, and the Magistrate of Sangkan, who followed Lord Lao to fathom the mysteries of the profound and dark. Vast and boundless, the Dao eludes all grasp—expansive as a valley, it embraces the ten thousand things. Broad and ever-flowing, it transcends the small and incomplete. It does not abandon simplicity, and in its vastness, all things find completion. To align with the times is the mechanism of rising above the mundane and entering sainthood; to hold fast to the center and embrace the One is the essence of learning.

The Primordial Yang Jade Calendar must be entrusted to the right person. The precious scriptures of the Most High condense the qi of spontaneity. When mortals recite them, their lives are prolonged; when spirits hear them, they ascend as immortals. Each bears the karmic causes of past lives, and thus their merits defy all reckoning.

We, your servant, though longing for the Dao, lack the talent of the worthy. We have not mastered the method of extracting lead and merging mercury in the golden elixir, yet we dare to undertake the duty of submitting sealed memorials. We reflect further on the Jiao leaders, who, sheltered by the divine, dwell in peace within their villages, honored at the shrine of Lingji. Endowed with wisdom and virtue, they bring timely sunshine and timely rain, fulfilling the auguries of tortoise and milfoil. Their merit serves the state, their blessings nourish the people—we recall the enduring joy inscribed on their monuments. Though millet and sorghum lack fragrance, we offer them in sacrifice. On the mornings of the Three Origins when blessings converge, we observe a day of fasting and abstinence. By the grace of the Heavenly Master above and the imperial favor below, we are adorned with honorific titles, our names resplendent. Such glory is unheard of in antiquity and unmatched in the present age.

This is all due to the august presence of the Jade Emperor of the Vast Heaven. The vault of Heaven arches above, the Emperor governs all—beneath his encompassing gaze, his benevolence has long been celebrated. We, your servant, are but lowly as ants and lice, foolish and dull. Only when we behold the celestial majesty of dragon and phoenix do we dare to speak. Though the divine may rely on talent, how could we idly occupy our positions? We must not fabricate affairs to seek merit. We have received more than our due—our gratitude is boundless. Yet we remain as one who clings to a tattered robe, ever mindful of treading on thin ice.

We humbly pray that your majesty’s virtue may endure for a hundred generations, that your blessings may descend in abundance, and that the imperial mandate may bestow prosperity upon all people. We, your servant, dare not cease in our reverence and awe. With this memorial, we respectfully express our gratitude.

**Memorial of Gratitude for the Bestowal of Rank at the Golden Palace**

Your servant [Name] humbly received the imperial decree on the first day of the third month, appointing me as the Nine Heavens Golden Palace Illuminated Dao and Virtuous Great Immortal, Manifest Spirit, and Universal Savior Zhenren, charged with overseeing the Upper Clarity Heavenly Texts Academy and all matters therein. Gazing toward the Golden Palace, we receive the imperial mandate—our new title inscribed upon the cinnabar terrace, our place secured among the immortal ranks. The radiance of this favor is profound, our awe and trepidation all the greater.

We, in awe and trepidation, bow our heads again and again. We reverently consider the Supreme Jade Clarity Palace, where all is carefree and joyous. Beyond lies the Mysterious True Realm, luminous and resplendent. Its symbols shine like the double halos of sun and moon, its auspicious signs weave through the five-colored mists. The myriad spirits pay homage, the Three Realms gather in attendance. Dragons and tigers array to the left and right, phoenixes and simurghs sing before and behind. This is the celestial realm’s delight—how could one of lowly station ever hear of it?

Through the revolutions of kalpas and the turning of the wheel, we awaken to the necessity of cultivating fasting and practicing the Dao, aspiring to attain sagehood and achieve perfection. We reflect that spirits are vast and unfathomable, while we dwell in the turbid world, rushing about. Sacrificing animals in worship, we know only the schemes of flesh-eaters.

The millet and sorghum are not fragrant; I humbly accept my place among those who partake of plain meals, clinging only to grass and trees. I have achieved no merit near or far, yet mistakenly received undeserved favor out of turn, belonging still to the ranks of witless spirits. From the Purple Tenuity Palace, the imperial edict is proclaimed; the Emperor’s Seat descends to the palace balcony. Its light approaches the Seven Stars, illuminating all within nine thousand li. My rank equals that of the constellations—numbering one hundred eighteen in all—overseeing the distribution of emoluments at the Three Terraces and assisting the Literary Prosperity in the Six Ministries. When virtue gathers, worthy men rejoice in assembly; when the Dipper overturns, the year’s grains yield abundance. The Old Man appears at the center of the Southern Culmen, below harmonizing with the Auspicious Staircase’s sign—all by the Emperor’s power, what merit is mine?

This is only because I have encountered the August Heavenly Jade Emperor beneath the Jade Steps. His great virtue is called "life," lofty and supreme; though without sound or scent, he is indeed possessed of form and image. With drums and banners, he once vowed to deliver humanity; holding the tally and wielding the calendar, he alone opened the origin of embodying the Dao. The cinnabar script revealed the essence of warmth and governance, while the green characters presented the auspicious omens of the Milky Way. Thunder issues decrees, the celestial river becomes his decree. Majestic is his descending might; he entrusts me with the selection of the Cultured Right. I, your servant, ascend the hall with sword and shoes, rejoicing in the worthy’s attainment, as the gowned and hatted come to court. I emulate the feudal lords’ offering of jade, deeply favored by grace, diligent in my duties.

I cannot contain my awe as I gaze upon the heavens and long for the sagely presence, overwhelmed with reverence. Humbly I present this memorial in gratitude.

**Memorial of Thanks for Accepting Office at the Jade Tower**

I, your servant, respectfully received on the first day of the third month the decree appointing me as the Nine Heavens Jade Tower Proclaiming Transformation and Upholding the Dao Supreme Immortal, Illustrious and Vastly Beneficent Perfected One, to govern all courts of the Lower Realm’s Earthly Prison and act with full authority. I prostrate myself before the solemn Jade Tower, bowing near the celestial steps; the golden script bestows honor, specially ennobling my appointment in the Earthly Prison. Overwhelmed by this private favor, I know not how to respond. Reverently I take my place, traversing countless millions of li. Uniting the Four Seas in shared custom, the twenty-eight lunar lodges encircle the heavens; corresponding to the Nine Provinces’ divisions, the three thousand worlds and all sentient beings are subject to the illumination of stars, sun, and moon. Whether forests, trees, mountains, or rivers—high or low—all are human: truly, how joyous!

I pray to open the purple sunlit cloud-brocade satchel and attain deliverance within the Jade Chamber’s cinnabar terrace. Though the Most High does not lightly bestow, I am fortunate that this humble servant may partake in hearing it. Day and night I press on, my spirit ever facing the divine. Reflecting, I am no ghost concealing myself but rely on others to act upon my thoughts. Though I wish to fulfill the heart of fasting and serving the Emperor, I remain subject to the reproach of gluttony and worthlessness. My fields are barren stone, my worldly ties unsevered. Mistakenly I have received the honor of imperial edicts and elegant decrees, specially entrusted with the people’s welfare. I exhort goodness and punish evil, penalize transgressions and reward merit. The virtuous have their names recorded in the Southern Palace; the guilty have their souls confined in the Northern Bureau. I oversee the immortal registers of the Three Isles’ sacred mountains and govern the true administrations of the Five Peaks and Four Continents.

Reverently I receive this solemn charge, trembling with awe. The flying squirrel must measure its strength; even the great turtle cannot bear such grace. This is only because I have encountered the August Jade Emperor of the Vast Heaven. The myriad forms flow into being, his favor reaches the utmost. He commands the transformations of yin’s gloom and yang’s ease, the powers of spring’s birth and autumn’s harvest. The Emperor’s chariot soars, the stars array in guard. The Dark Capital stretches boundlessly, adorned with the seven treasures. Auspiciousness unfolds in the azure vault’s hymns; I look up to praise the Jade Emperor’s august title. Repeatedly I have received his gracious commands, surpassing my peers. Ashamed of my lack of merit, I have been elevated—my body cleansed, my sincerity already expressed in offerings of pondweed and water plants. In divining harvests and praying for the year, there is the joy of millet, sorghum, rice, and grains. Below, I fulfill the people’s wishes; above, I answer the heavens’ intent.

I cannot contain my gratitude for this grace, overwhelmed with reverence. Humbly I present this memorial in gratitude, performing the rites with reverent words.

**Memorial to the Heavenly Master**

It seems your virtue has long sheltered the southern Min, while I gaze toward the northern palace, once more beholding the sun and moon’s light. The imperial decree’s favor descends, and I blush in self-reproach. I am truly fearful and awestruck, bowing my head again and again.

I have heard that Mount Ci once manifested its form at the river’s edge, receiving the great emperor’s enfeoffment in the catalpa shrine. Reverently it descended its brush upon Min and E, extravagantly celebrating the Primordial Emperor’s praise. Through filial piety and sincerity, heroic deeds attain the Dao; through woodcutting and smelting, compassionate aid achieves success. If not for vowing to deliver humanity, how could one transcend the mundane and enter sageliness? Such things exist—how could they be mere chance?

Turning to my own conduct, only the Dao is great. Since the Great Ultimate’s division, there have been the people and the altars of state. By the end of the five kalpas, who shall uphold the guiding principles? This is only because I have encountered the Orthodox Unity, Tranquil Response, Divine Transformation, Manifest Assistance Perfected Lord. When the heart can respond with tranquility and attain the Dao, silently merging with the divine and transforming, it is effortless non-action; when manifesting assistance, it is as if abundantly present. His aspiration is to aid the state and pacify the people; his heart is to establish teachings and set forth regulations. Purple characters and golden names mark the registers of medicinal pearls; jade seals and vermilion tallies translate the phoenix-script texts. The Dao’s law precedes heaven, its learning transmitted to later ages. The hundred spirits guard it; the myriad things revere it. The Great Mystery’s fifteen govern the world from Ghost Valley; the Supreme Yang’s First Administration corresponds to the Horn Star. His numinosity shines through antiquity, his deeds recorded in historical transmissions—beyond the contemplation of one such as I. This is why the Master’s Dao is uniquely revered.

Reflecting, I, your servant, rely on others to act, clinging only to the divine. I am akin to rotting grass, a decaying tree without pattern. My stele inscriptions are doubly shamed by Lord Liu; my posthumous name barely survives in Jin history. I cannot distinguish medicine from stone, much less know of Ma Fu or Niu Sou; my furnace and tripod are incomplete—how could I recognize dragon lead or tiger mercury? Though I possess the will to save things, I initially lack the talent to order the world. In divining like Junping and practicing auspicious arts, I merely instruct in loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and righteousness, following the teachings of Confucius.

Still, critics admonish me—marvels, powers, and spirits disrupt the Dao, and by these I scheme. Unaware of what I emulate, I have long called such reckless acts a sin from which no earth affords escape. Who could have foreseen that undeserved grace would fall from heaven, that honors would elevate my rank, that I would ascend the immortal ranks, receiving this as if it were my due? To gain it truly startles me. Adrift on the sea of the great leviathan, my spirit flees and my soul trembles; bearing the mountain of the giant turtle, my virtue swells with profound favor. Since assuming office, I have remained as cautious as at first. Upholding the rites of repentance and admonition, I know my own recklessness and fail to grasp the essence of scriptural teachings—yet I still hope for enlightenment. All this stems from my master’s transmission; how dare I claim it as my own achievement? I revere the sagely transformation and proclaim the winds of benevolence. Above, I pray for the sovereign’s longevity, echoing the triple invocation of Mount Song; below, I ensure my people receive the blessings of the *Ji Chou*, as the talismanic transmissions foretell. May sons beget grandsons, and grandsons beget sons in unbroken succession. Though the rites of pepper and orchid may lapse, only the Dao resides in the heart, and the heart is the Dao. Even dogs and horses know to love their master—how could ants and crickets fail to convey their devotion? My heart brims with longing for grace, to the point of trembling awe.

I, your servant, now submit this memorial in gratitude.

**Memorial of Gratitude to the Heavenly Master and True Lord for Appointment**

I have heard that the Dao’s vastness is called greatness, beginning in emptiness, tranquility, and non-action. The spirit attains oneness and becomes numinous, discerning advance and retreat, life and death, without losing its correctness. When its emanations all strike true, who enables this? Is it not the karmic thread of past good fortune, allowing one to seize the moment and awaken?

I, your servant, offer my thanks: I observe that the Nine Heavens’ Numinous Aid Perfected One is upright in humanity and enlightened in divinity. Not merely scheming for sealed

**Memorial of Congratulation to the Sacred Father, Prince Qi, the Loyal and Martial Perfected One**

With reverence, we reflect upon Your Highness, the Sacred Father, Prince Qi, the Loyal and Martial Perfected One: repaying the state with loyalty, establishing merit through martial prowess. Selecting households for enfeoffment, you have long received the favor of the jade tablet’s grace. Issuing royal decrees, you once unsealed the golden casket’s writ. Your might shook the Huai and Yangtze, your blessings descended upon the garrisoned commanderies. Yesterday, the offering of winter-blooming camellia brought forth purple qi that filled the court; today, the auspicious omen of the blue arrow’s light illumined the chamber. We, your humble servants, though unworthy to stand in your shadow, have yet to fully bask in your boundless grace. Gazing toward the northern palace, we pour forth our devotion; pointing to the southern mountains, we pray for your longevity. We further hope that in the hall’s joyous feasting, all may nurture hearts of familial harmony; that within the four borders, peace may reign, and everywhere, the divine hemp’s shelter be enjoyed. We present this memorial in congratulation.

Moreover, as the new year begins in harmony, its auspiciousness is confirmed by the dawning day. The Nine Heavens resound with celebration, and all rejoice together in the praise of the divine. Auspicious qi drifts like clouds, while joyful voices thunder like thunder. I, your servant, in awe and trepidation, bow my head again and again to offer congratulations.

With reverence, we reflect upon Your Highness, the Sacred Father, Prince Qi, the Loyal and Martial Perfected One: your nature is upright and just, your rule both martial and civil. Once, your name was heard beyond the Yangtze; now, your deeds flourish in the heart of Min. The four directions’ worthies gather like crowns and tiaras; the radiance of sun and moon is doubled. For a thousand ages, incense and lamps endure, as eternal as heaven and earth. We bow our heads in homage, emulating the reverence of Zhao Hu; we raise our cups in toast, following the example of Ni Kuan. Thus, we practice the rustic rites and extend the village feast. There are those of high and low station, elders and youths—none dare transgress. They seek longevity, wealth, ease, and peace, each according to their prayers. We humbly present this memorial in congratulation.

I, your servant, in utmost joy and exultation, bow my head again and again. My heart brims with fervent devotion, earnest and unwavering.

---

**Memorial from the Southern Palace on Behalf of a Man Seeking Peace and Well-Being**

I have heard that the great Dao is without action—who can fathom the myriad mysteries of its profound profundity? Those who receive its deliverance may hope to endure through kalpas without end. Such truths are not for ordinary mortals to hear; only the virtuous are blessed with its fortune.

I observe that so-and-so conducts himself with frugality and humility, his nature upright and gentle. Yet, by an ill-fated alignment of the stars, he has suffered the afflictions of *Shichen*’s malevolence. Through earnest supplication, he has at last found relief from his ailments. Now, in the year of his sixtieth cycle, he encounters his natal day, though his appearance—his hair thinned, his vigor diminished—no longer matches his former self. Though aged and feeble, he is fortunate that the luminous Perfected One has granted him favor. The scriptures revealed from the Jade Bureau offer nothing but texts to dispel misfortune; the teachings expounded upon the Millet Pearl are all canons to deliver humanity. Such merits and virtues may serve as a bridge to salvation.

I, your servant, though unworthy among the Dao’s followers and presumptuous in performing ritual affairs, have contributed not even a fraction of the primordial work’s merit. How dare I repeatedly present my foolish petitions? With reverence, we reflect upon the Sacred Throne of the Southern Palace’s August Emperor: your benevolence is vast and your mercy boundless, your merits untainted by fault. You govern the nine yang’s mysteries, your Sanskrit vows forming the three caverns’ numinous power. The literary tablets record the embryos and forms of all beings; once endowed with shape and visage, you surely safeguard their lives, cherish their spirits, and ensure that the root of the numinous is watered, its branches flourishing and leaves abundant. You cause the primordial fluid to congeal and solidify, its source deep and its flow far-reaching. Let neither joy nor anger, nor pleasure’s excess, disturb our nature; let neither right nor wrong, nor gain nor loss, confuse our hearts.

Ascending to the Supreme Mystery, severing all perverse obstructions.
Inscribing names on cinnabar tablets, recording words in azure scriptures.
Above, we trace the grace of the Great Unity; below, we console the hopes of the people.
We humbly pray that white may reverse to black, outwardly transmitting the formula of agelessness;
That qi may turn from purple to embrace yellow, inwardly attaining the secret of eternal life.
Further, we hope that all households flourish in prosperity, their descendants thriving in abundance.
Also, on behalf of women engaging in preemptive cultivation—

We reverently consider: *The Scripture of the Yellow Court*, a single classic, emerged from the Fusang Palace, where we beseech to hear the Lady Wei’s expositions.
The three volumes of numinous writ descended upon the Cheng Hua Hall, joyfully receiving the Queen Mother of the West’s direct transmission.
These may extend our years and serve to establish teachings and regulations.

We reflect that though this servant has reached the age of sixty, my learning remains unworthy of mention. Unaware of the li and kan within myself, how can I fathom the great transformations of Heaven and Earth?
Yet, by the grace of the true shade, I have concealed myself in the mysteries of the Daoist codes. With deeper consideration, I recall the female disciple [Name], who, with her five-leaky body, dwells in the mundane world, merely indulging in frivolous laughter, nearly reducing goodness to ruin.
Her merit, appearance, speech, and virtue—none of the four teachings are complete.
Joy and anger, a single morning’s pleasure, the six emotions all encumbered.

In the year of *jihai*, coinciding with the seventh evening’s beginning,
The *gengshen* rites are recorded, yet I still fear the lurking Three Corpses.
Reverently facing the heavens, I submit this plea in proxy,
Resolving from this day forth to renew myself.
May the crown of my head become the cause of blessings,
And may I humbly beseech unseen assistance.

I reverently consider the August Emperor of Southern Florescence of Nanchang,
The Great Emperor of Longevity of the Southern Pole,
And the Life-Cherishing Lord Han, the Venerable Man—
Their transformative radiance manifests in the Eight Luminaries,
Their Dao pervades the Three Spirits.
Ten recitations of scripture deliver humankind;
Nine Yangs are refined into qi.
Vast and majestic their model,
Serene and boundless their origin.

I implore the Three Realms to descend as one,
To record your merits and erase your transgressions.
May the multitude of perfected ones be indiscriminately delivered,
Preserving your life and honoring your form,
Enabling you to endure through kalpas and abide long.
Daring to seize this moment of awakening,
I gaze toward the northern palace in hope of grace,
That my name be inscribed in the southern archives,
Receiving the texts of yellow threads and white tablets,
Etched in purple characters and golden names.
May your years be prolonged,
Eight thousand seasons turning as spring and autumn.
Bestow upon me boundless favor,
A hundred generations flourishing with descendants.
Above, embody the Supreme’s virtue of cherishing life;
Below, regard this servant’s earnest entreaty.

Gratitude to the master for recommending the completion of merit for the departed.
I have heard with joy of the *Western Ascension*,
Transmitted by Lord Lao,
And of the covenant rites receiving the *Yellow Emperor’s Questions on the Yin Talisman*,
Expounded by Guangchengzi.
Faithfully received and reverently practiced.
Were it not for karmic predestination,
How could one possess the bone-form of an immortal?

This servant, trembling with awe,
Bows his head again and again.
I reflect that my canine-and-horse years have reached eighty;
Though now aged, I remain capable of one final endeavor.
The dragon-and-phoenix scriptures—I have studied but two or three.
Yet even a fool, it is said, may achieve insight through a thousand considerations.
Since assuming this office,
I have guarded the Dao with strictness.
How can I discipline others
Without first demanding it of myself?
Talent must be tested:
Those with merit are rewarded,
Those with transgressions are punished.
Thus may all act with sincerity in virtue,
And prudence in speech.

I reverently consider the Perfected Lord of Orthodox Unity, Tranquil Response, and Manifest Protection—
His dharma transmitted as Orthodox Unity,
His Dao penetrating the subtle mysteries.
For ten thousand generations, he is the teacher of rulers,
The parent of all living beings.
He establishes teachings and regulations,
The Great Dharma Master of All Heavens,
Pointing the way to salvation and deliverance,
Rescuing the suffering and liberating the departed,
Awakening the vow of compassion.

Yet I fear that the spirits thus recommended,
Adrift in the turbid currents of fleeting life,
May have unwittingly committed errors.
In the endless night’s darkness,
Who recognizes the marvel of emerging from existence and entering non-existence?
Only through merit may this serve as a bridge.

I humbly pray that the Great Dao illuminate,
The earth be purged of demonic vapors,
The heavens free of drifting haze,
Soul and spirit purified and rectified.
Let the smoke-choked gates of death open,
The clouds part to reveal the gates of life.
May even the darkest yin realms
All receive the mysterious grace.

**Refinement and Deliverance Memorial**

I prostrate myself, for at the center of the Azure Heaven,
The *Scripture of Deliverance* is proclaimed.
After the kalpa of the August Emperor,
The *Stanzas of the Divine Generative Spirit* were covenanted.
As the great cycle nears its term,
The sacred texts emerge.

This servant, trembling with fear,
Reflects that my heart remains enslaved to things,
My body not yet merged with the true.
I have not heard of the tortoise-breathing method,
And deeply shame at my crane-hair and dragon-decrepitude.
Yet I lead the prayers with utmost sincerity,
Striving to practice diligently.

I fear that the departed spirits thus recommended,
Sunk in the dust of worldly illusion,
Entangled in emotional attachments,
May have unwittingly committed errors of thought, word, or intent.
Returning to the root and restoring the origin—
Who recognizes the marvel of essence, qi, and spirit?
Self-inflicted is the ruin of death;
Who knows the path to life?

I reverently consider the Great Emperor of the Divine Generative Spirit of the Nine Heavens—
His Dao pervades the Three Spirits,
His transformative power flows through the Two Luminaries.
In the East, he is known as the Great Compassionate and Great Merciful.
In Nanchang, he oversees the bureaus of Deliverance and Refinement.
Yin becomes po, yang becomes hun—
Only through yin and yang are they tempered.
Fire pertains to the heart, water to the kidneys—
Without water and fire, how could life be formed?

I implore the Great Creation to embrace all,
The true light to illumine thoroughly,
That the foul and putrid be utterly dissolved,
The withered and decayed, upon hearing, emit smoke.
May bones and flesh take flight together,
Form and spirit be made whole.
Inner thoughts not stray outward,
Outer thoughts not intrude within,
Forever cutting off the source of afflictions.
Once the register of qi is established,
And the qi of compliance is born,
A body of empty cavernousness emerges.
May all suffering souls
Bathe in this vast grace.

Moreover, the *Scripture of Deliverance*,
Recited ten times, revives withered bones.
The *Stanzas of the Divine Generative Spirit*,
Comprising nine chapters, liberates dark souls.
The Supreme attained this
To establish teachings and regulations.
Later students rely on it
To rescue the suffering and deliver the departed.

I reverently consider the sacred ranks—
Seven epochs aligned,
Three Spirits conjoined,
Above embodying the creative transformations of Heaven and Earth.
Yin employs the even, yang the odd;
Within, the work of *li* and *kan* is illuminated.
Water seeks the damp, fire the dry.
A bridge for the multitude of sufferings,
A sun and moon for the lost multitudes.
My vows are profound,
My merit boundless.

I reflect that in recent years, old and senile,
My studies have grown neglected.
Tiger mercury and dragon lead—
I have not mastered the ninefold transmutations and completions.
Bear postures and tortoise breathing—
I know not the method of one inhalation and one exhalation.
Yet when I previously received the memorial,
I fulfilled my allotted duty.
Now, witnessing the filial devotion’s sincerity,
I reluctantly undertake the rites to preside over them.

I deeply consider the departed souls thus recommended—
Yesterday they possessed living bodies,
Today they enter the register of the dead.
Below, their hun and po are summoned,
Long wandering in the springs’ curves.
Knocking on skulls,
They have only recently found the joy of returning to their native mounds.
Without undergoing the refining furnace,
How can they transcend the ordinary?

I implore the Three Realms to descend as one,
The multitude of perfected ones to descend,
To deliver the dead souls for refinement,
Enabling them to transform into immortals.
Merging marvelously, dissolving forms,
Their kind dispersed across kalpas
Return to the One.
They must rely on the power of ascending the primordial,
Encountering the work of Brahma.

Moreover, in the Azure Vault of Floating Li,
The ten recitations of the *Scripture of Deliverance* are expounded.
From the Jade Terrace of Primordial Yang,
The nine stanzas of the *Divine Generative Spirit* emerge.
Since the transmission of these teachings,
Through successive masters and disciples.

I reflect that this servant, humbly among later students,
Has inherited the governance of the mysterious codes.
Yet I do not understand *li* and *kan* within myself,
Nor comprehend the creative transformations of Heaven and Earth.
Still, I lead the prayers with utmost sincerity,
Striving to practice diligently.

Deeply I fear that the departed souls,
misled between past lives and deaths to come,
may have erred in their ways.
Some, succumbing to incurable ulcers,
are deemed to suffer karmic retribution—
yet where does the *po* soul wander?
Who guards the *hun* and sustains the *po*?
The form is no longer theirs—
who can refine the substance and temper the body?
Without the aid of incense and cultivation,
by what means can they transcend?

I reverently recall the sacred ranks:
empty and formless, they transform naturally.
They perceive the radiance of the Eight Luminaries,
and silently align with the Seven Mysteries in reverence.
The deliverance of the netherworld weighs heavily upon my vows.
I humbly beseech:
summon them through yin, call them through yang,
that the dead souls may undergo refinement.
Disperse them with wind, moisten them with rain,
that withered bones may be revived.

Moreover,
the Most High has bequeathed scriptures for the deliverance of souls,
while I, a minor official of scattered duties,
possess no talent for memorializing.
Bound by my station, what can I say?
Overwhelmed, I dare not falter.
I offer my gratitude, reverently recalling the sacred ranks:
they uphold Heaven’s ordinances, embody the Emperor’s radiance.
Though they seem distant and obscure,
who knows their ceaseless transformations?
Those who receive *qi* return to the bellows and bellows-bag;
those endowed with form emerge from the potter’s mold.
Breathing life into the withered, exhaling upon the decayed,
they silently master the wonders of yin and yang.
Above, they blaze; below, they moisten—
looking up, I fathom the workings of water and fire.
The formless can manifest in form;
the true sovereign acts without sovereign intent.
Their luminous, mighty deeds
deliver boundless beings.

I reflect upon the patron of this rite, a certain woman of this day,
whose heart aches with grief, tears flowing from her sorrow,
as she mourns her daughter’s untimely death.
Before eight days had passed, she was struck by her husband’s demise,
parting forever beneath the heavens.
This sorrow, this love—
nowhere to express, nowhere to plead.
I trust that King Wen’s grace
can extend even to withered bones.
Yet I, a mere alchemist, am ashamed—
my learning falls short of the divine elixir’s mysteries.
Still, following the guidance of the enlightened present,
the true souls may yet be delivered.

The Dao of Heaven perfects the male;
the Dao of Earth perfects the female.
Trace their origins, befriend their ends.
Moonlight becomes the *po*;
sunlight becomes the *hun*.
They inscribe your life, erase your death.

**Memorial for Redemption of Sins**

Rank is not to be profaned;
punishment is not to be trifled with.
All covet rank—
why then do they not fear punishment?
Merit is weighty;
sin is light.
Who examines merit to redeem sin?
All is self-inflicted.
If one acts in ignorance,
were it not for the Most High’s love of life,
the people would perish utterly.
Thus, the purple clouds of dawn unfurl,
and the pearl of millet is hung aloft,
granting absolution for transgressions,
rescuing the departed from suffering.
The tally is struck, amnesty proclaimed,
that the Three Offices and Nine Bureaus
may inspect the ghostly camps and expound the law.
Hearing the scriptures, countless spirits ascend,
and ten thousand ancestors take flight.
By this merit, the Golden Towers stand;
virtue becomes the bridge.

I reflect that I, with decayed teeth and hoary head,
am a pitiable, doddering figure.
Low in rank and humble in duty,
I am as clumsy as a lame horse.
Yet, charged with this office, I must speak and present my case.
Like a rat stirring at night,
I fear only being seen—
great shame would be my disgrace.
I would fall in terror, saved only by heaven’s grace.
I humbly beseech that my loyal sincerity be seen,
and the weight of a filial child’s devotion be recognized.
Today, I act on behalf of a grieving daughter, so-and-so,
who mourns her late father, so-and-so.
Since his self-inflicted death,
three years have passed,
and though she has long wished to perform rites,
her hopes remain unfulfilled.

I observe that the departed soul,
succumbing to an incurable ulcer,
was ultimately misled by the Two Fiends.
His heart was not deceitful—
why then was he drawn toward the Three Corpses?
Sincere words stirred, yet
it was said his hidden yin virtue was lacking.
Thus, he fell into the netherworld,
unable to awaken or understand.
Alas, the barrier between the living and the dead—
not something ears or eyes can perceive.
In the depths of prison,
even Gongye Chang was innocent.
To suffer as Dong Zhongshu did,
or endure the humiliation of Sima Qian—
was there no regret?

I, who have presumptuously taken office in the yang realm,
know nothing of yin’s laws.
To cleanse others,
I must first confront my own fears.
My voice, like thunder’s echo,
is but the caw of a crow that thinks itself loud.
Gazing to the ends of rivers and seas,
am I not like a fish that has slipped the net?
The Lü Clan once scrutinized the Five Punishments and Five Penalties,
while the *Rites of Zhou* spoke of Three Pardons and Three Amnesties.
Lacking Mulan’s filial piety,
how dare I presume to present a petition like Lady Tiying’s?
Like a moth drawn to flame,
where can I find refuge?
Like a stray dog without a home,
my plight is truly pitiable.

I reverently recall the sacred ranks:
they vow compassion,
responding to cries and answering pleas,
honored as the Most Unique of the Great One.
Their light shines universally across the Three Thousand Worlds,
to the easternmost reaches.
In the Wondrous and Solemn Palace,
they manifest in purple-golden form.
The Great Mystery knows no bounds—
I have heard of the *Scripture of the Great Cavern*.
Wishing to be a bridge for all beings,
they rescue from every suffering.

I humbly beseech:
swiftly erase the ledgers of sin,
and relocate his spirit to the Northern Mansion.
Select from the ranks of immortals,
and inscribe his name in the Southern Palace.
Let the winds of immortals carry his merit—
thus concludes the ninth scroll of *Xu Xian’s Elegant Writings*.
The tenth scroll of *Xu Xian’s Elegant Writings* begins.

Four Prayers for Peace

In this second month of mid-spring, all people pray for renewal, and the August Heavenly Lord does not forsake us. With a single heart we may reach the divine; our shared plea ascends, piercing the ninefold heavens.

We, the lowly, cling to life like ants and grubs, yet know gratitude. Though we dwell beneath the vast canopy of heaven and earth, our days pass in restless haste, untouched by the burdens of right and wrong. Searching our hearts, we find few who recognize their faults; reviewing our deeds, we see many who have wrought harm. Ever mindful of our fears, we dare rely on the power of this single offering.

May the gods above and below witness our virtue and guide us left and right. May farmers, artisans, merchants, and scholars rejoice in their livelihoods—thus shall they prosper.

---

The common people, ignorant, often invoke blessings through borrowed spirits. Yet the Heavenly Lord watches over you, without partiality in rewarding merit or punishing wrong. If He does not deceive us, aid will come to those who act in accord with the Way.

We, the humble, dwell by the mountains, hewing homes from stone and carving fields from slopes. As the stars of the Crow and the Winnowing Basket appear in mid-spring, we begin our labors in earnest. The barking of dogs carries across the four borders, and we long for the Great Stem. Knowing the hardship of earning our sustenance, we dare not withhold our sincerity in offering thanks.

Though we are frogs at the bottom of a well, unable to grasp the vastness of the world, even ants clinging to a cauldron deserve pity for their lives. May planting and weeding, from this day forward, yield harvests year after year. May peace and wealth—desires of all hearts—be granted by Heaven. Further, we pray for the flourishing of our cattle and livestock, truly bearing the weight of your boundless grace and nurturing care.

---

The will of the people is plain to see: their gaze and hearing are near, for they are the people themselves.

The Emperor’s command cannot be defied; with fasting and purification, we may offer sacrifice to the Emperor. Earnest in our pleas, we stand as though in the presence of His radiant majesty. We humbly reflect that we, like ants clinging to a cauldron or frogs at the bottom of a well, are greedy and shallow. Born in the Central Land, we have yet to fulfill our duties to our satisfaction. Now, as the Upper Prime arrives, we still hope for the blessings of the Heavenly Officials. Thus, we rely upon the Daoist adept to proclaim the true rites, reaching upward to the stern judgment of the axe and iron, and downward to the ears of even the lowliest creatures. Though the present may not know the past, we are fortunate that even impure customs may be renewed.

We pray that those like the Earl of Shen and the Marquis of Fu may rise again, and that those who follow may attain the longevity of Peng and the wealth of Tao, assuredly receiving such blessings. In all our movements and undertakings, we are truly indebted to the virtue of creation and nurture.

---

In this sixtieth year, on the day of my birth:
The Dao ever favors the good, and one must understand the causes of goodness. Our desire for peace has been fulfilled, and our wish for tranquility granted. Respectfully relying upon the Daoist adept, we present these written prayers. We humbly reflect that though my words are unworthy, I have now reached the age of ear-turning. Once afflicted with the ailment of gathering firewood, I now enjoy the blessing of recovery without medicine. Moreover, as the tenth month arrives, I mark my birth once more. Truly, I am indebted to the decree of Heaven and dare not betray my former vows. I pray that my later years may be prosperous and smooth, offering my sincere heart in gratitude. The merit of this act may be measured, and my reverence is as solemn as the fear of the tiger. May my ancestors rest in peace, their memory honored without fail. Looking upward, I seek divine aid; bowing downward, I beg for confirmation.

---

**Thanksgiving Prayer by a Woman for Preemptive Merit**
Rites, when overly elaborate, lead to disorder; only utmost sincerity can move the gods. Heaven guides the heart, and the accumulation of good deeds brings abundant blessings. Looking upward, we beseech the celestial hearing; bowing downward, we reveal our tender sentiments. We humbly reflect that I, your servant, lack the Four Virtues and that my many words are of little benefit. My learning is as unclear as the misreading of "three pigs," and now I approach the years beyond sixty, nearing seventy. My voice is as insignificant as a single fly, yet I fear repeating past mistakes. Removing my hairpin in submission, I gather my robes and present these words, repenting for past transgressions and cultivating future blessings. Further, I pray that my descendants, countless generations hence, may be enrolled in the register of Han Jun. May the Three Longevities be my companions, and may I receive the ode of Lu Hou.

---

**Preemptive Prayer by a Woman for the Yellow Register and Celestial Decree**
Human nature may incline toward good or evil, and even a foolish woman may comprehend this. Our desires for longevity and peace are met with Heaven’s favor, which brings only auspiciousness. Bowing low, I offer my enduring reverence; looking upward, I dare to disturb Your majestic countenance. We humbly reflect that I, your wife, am entangled in the desires of the world and submerged in the dust of the mundane. The five defilements of form and sound have surely brought their share of offenses. Though my hair is half-gray, I am fortunate to have reached the year of my birth once more. Overwhelmed and at a loss, I can only repent and give thanks inadequately. Respectfully, on the second day of the second month, I reverently partake in the rites of the Three Realms’ covenant with the true, dedicating the fruits of my merit in hope of Your grace. May this offering extend to my lord, deepening the love that binds us. May my later years be brightened, and may I further seek the joy of playful delight.

---

**Ritual Prayer for Thanksgiving**
As the year marks my sixtieth cycle, I find myself at this appointed time. My emotions struggle to reach the heavens, and I cannot avoid repeating my pleas. Rites must not be neglected, and words are spoken when the time is right. We humbly reflect that I, old and feeble, am without ability, confused and unenlightened. Recently afflicted with the lowly ailments of horses and cattle, I cried out to Heaven in desperation. Now, clinging to life like an ant, how can I not be moved by the earth’s compassion? Though my good intentions have taken shape in words, I am fortunate that the radiant gods may perceive my heart. Bowing low, I express my private gratitude; looking upward, I dare to disturb Your exalted hearing. As merit is fulfilled, may my name be inscribed in the golden register and white tally. May I be granted the blessings of abundance, longevity, health, and peace, as bestowed by the *Hong Fan* and *Ji Chou*. Further, I pray that my descendants may bring glory to their forebears.

---

**Prayer for the Ancestral Mother’s Protection**
To know gratitude is to know repayment; the August Heaven and Earth indeed hear our solemn words. To serve the dead as we serve the living is the duty of filial sons and obedient grandsons. Thus, we rely upon this pure rite, presumptuously beseeching the true banner. We humbly reflect that I was orphaned at four and received instruction through three relocations. In the past, through my grandmother, I suffered from an incurable blindness; my late father was deeply grieved by my drowning, yet could not save me. Though I repeatedly prayed to the gods, why did misfortune still befall me? Unfortunate in my short life, I wept as I recounted my unfulfilled vows, knowing not how to proceed. Fortunately, over the years, I have come to terms with my fate, easing my heart and freeing it from its initial burdens. The departed flow like this river, and may they soon align with Han Jun’s compassionate work. In the end, may there be care, and may the ode of Lu Hou praising a mother’s longevity be sung.

---

**Prayer for a Wife**
When illness strikes, one calls to Heaven, for there is no other recourse. If dreams bring harm, we seek to understand their cause. Bowing low, I pour forth my sincerity; looking upward, I beseech the celestial hearing. We humbly reflect that I am bound by fate to the Dipper’s middle star, and my affairs are as discordant as Shen and Shang. Lamenting the hardships of my household, why are my family’s fortunes so fraught? Even beasts do not lose their mates—how could I lack the sentiments of the world? Though the bowstring may be rejoined, I cannot avoid new attachments. Despite the ugliness of painted brows and powdered cheeks, why am I afflicted by the misfortune of arrows piercing my chest? Perhaps the love and hate of the reed mat differ, rendering the healing of medicine ineffective. Thus, I have pledged to invoke the True Man of Lingji, proclaiming the repentance of the Nine Truths. I pray that the Most High Lord of the Great Monad may widely bestow His great compassion, releasing me from karmic transgressions and delivering me from suffering. Alas, my former wife—early did she fulfill the cause of the trailing tail. May my descendants be preserved, forever upholding the duty of the silken threads.

---

Moreover:
Heaven’s brightness is to be revered, for its power is manifest in what is seen and heard—how could it lack ears and eyes?

Where matters arise from nothingness, oaths and curses invoke the unseen—yet how can one bind the spirits of ghosts and gods? To believe so is folly indeed.

I, so-and-so, reflect in shame: my conduct has strayed from propriety, my ignorance as dull as the crawling of insects. Like a bandit breaching the inner gate, my voice went unheard even by the barking dogs. A wife’s loose tongue, like the clucking of a hen, truly invites scorn. What was taken in the rites must be returned—reason demands self-reproach. Yet if suffering arises from negligence, who would deny the cry of injustice? Rewarding good and punishing excess—swift as echo follows sound. To untie resentment and loosen knots, one may yet find refuge in the rites of repentance.

Moreover:
Heaven cannot be deceived—its gaze is lofty, its ears ever near. When man’s wrath stirs, it wells from the heart and takes shape in words. How can it be otherwise? One must seek its cause.

I, so-and-so, as a person, now ponder: recalling my late father, he clung to the folly of the waiting tree-stump, never expecting treachery to strike like a stone cast from below. I appealed to the August Emperor to judge right and wrong, and by good fortune, the courts rendered clarity. Ashamed of my clumsy pleas, how dare I betray my sworn vows? Humble and base as I am, I now approach the pure hall to offer rites of apology. My feeble efforts scarcely begin to repay the debt—yet if I delay further, I fear my resolve may waver again.

Flaws may be renewed as the sun and moon recover from eclipse; what use is brightness if it invites the censure of the *Spring and Autumn*'s unflinching brush?

**Establishing the Altar of the Mysterious Capital: Petition**

On the fifteenth day of the seventh month in the autumn of the *renxu* year, we reverently welcome the Earth Official on the day of his audit and recording.

The Mandate of Heaven is stern toward the people below. First, we exhaust the rites of purification and luminous reverence, arranging fragrant mats to humbly lodge our modest sincerity.

We reflect: our blood and *qi* share the same origin as all flesh. Though our departed kin could but offer the devotion of dogs and horses, how dare we forget the gratitude of crows and magpies? Time flows like this river—yet we err in composing these summoning verses. Yet if faults can be dissolved, we have heard it may be done in the space between turning palms.

Respectfully following the Mysterious Code, we solemnly invite the feathered adepts to perform these meritorious deeds and establish this karmic connection.

We humbly pray that the Three Officials of the Northern Fengdu may scrutinize the ghostly camps and swiftly expunge the ledgers of sin. May our countless ancestors ascend to the Golden Gates, each finding their path to rebirth. May all the lost and deluded together attain joy and liberation.

**Prayer for Averting Disaster**

Harmonious *qi* brings auspiciousness, while discordant *qi* brings anomalies—Heaven’s ways are inscrutable and without constancy. The Way of fortune lengthens as the Yin Way wanes; the return of the sun may be awaited.

We bow in lowly submission and gaze upward in presumptuous address.

We reflect: though we have fortunately secured safety, we have failed to maintain it. Though the multitudes petition for disaster-averting rites, we petty folk know the shame of our transgressions. None dares face the sunflower’s devotion; we can but fear the depths of the abyss. How can our village compare? We have but a humble puddle’s worth of reverence.

Thus we gather the Daoist clergy to solemnly conduct the ritual. We trust the people’s plight is easily seen and pray the Emperor’s wrath may be turned.

We humbly beseech that sand be transformed into harmony, sparing us the dread of neglected sacrifices. May we be granted longevity and prosperity, and may abundant blessings descend.

**Prayer for Preserving Fortune**

The Way of Heaven speaks not, yet responds—we offer our earnest supplications. The human heart’s desires, when sincere, must surely evoke a resonant response.

We inscribe this in our hearts, knowing our debt is profound.

We reflect: we, so-and-so, rely solely upon the divine, having no merits to recount. Yet we have been doubly favored by Heaven’s bounty and honored by our master’s grace. Recently, we entrusted Chen Daoxing with the *Dragon-Tiger* rites, and indeed received great protection. Now, with Elder Guo Yong, we fulfill the *Cricket’s* repayment, refusing to renege on our word.

Though this is the people’s hope, how dare we claim any credit for Heaven’s power? We further pray for the bestowal of the *gui zan* scepter, that we may await summons in the Purple Tenuity, and for the offering of fine grains, that the spirits may be at peace in the Pure Temple.

**Establishing the Ritual of Crossing: Petition**

The Heavenly Worthy expounded the teachings, pointing the way to salvation. For children honoring their parents, the foremost path is filial reverence.

We bow in earnest address, gazing upward to the azure vault.

We reflect: we, so-and-so, dwell in the dust. Though we have fortunately lived through the final kalpa, we recall those who bore and raised us, whose nurturing love was as deep as the canopy of heaven. Yet they linger between existence and oblivion—how hateful is the barrier between light and dark! Thus we rely on the feathered adepts to perform the true rites.

Today, we open the Mysterious Altar, seeking to ascend our prayers to the Imperial Palace. May our humble sincerity move the divine, and may great proof be granted.

Words cannot express our joy: the assembled hosts from the ten directions witness the deliverance of the living and the dead. By the grace bestowed upon the nine hundred, all hearts are poured forth. May the lost in the underworld all ascend to the shore of the Dao.

**Moreover,**

The hearing of Heaven is impartial; may it deign to perceive even a fraction of our foolish sincerity.

Here is the translation, maintaining consistency with the previous section’s style and terminology:

---

When rites grow excessive, they breed disorder—how deeply we fear the repeated offense of overburdening the divine, lest we incur fault through our own urgency. Yet there are matters that admit no delay.

We reflect: though we are but gnats in nature, ants in survival, each possesses a human heart—how could we lack good intentions? Now, as the Zhongyuan Festival approaches, we begin our fast eight days prior, wishing to forge karmic bonds with all beings. Thus we undertake the Nine Mornings’ Universal Deliverance, humbly invoking sacred power and beseeching the bestowal of gracious light. We dare offer our private gratitude, striving to manifest reverence from beginning to end. Further, we pray for the five viscera to be cleansed and cool, the six bowels harmonized and at peace. May the old regain their vigor, the young grow strong. May the Three Realms provide guardianship, the Five Emperors oversee their reception. May the *po* ascend, the *hun* be liberated.

Moreover,
Though Heaven’s height seems boundless, it never strays from the square inch of the heart. As mortals, we must be vigilant from the outset, ever mindful of the perils of neglecting the fast. Following the Yellow Register’s rites, we draw near to the purple radiance to invoke the sacred. Deeply reliant on the vast creation’s workings, we open wide the path of salvation. May the darkness of the underworld be illuminated, the long night ended, and the light of Yang Valley be beheld—each soul restored to spring.

**Second Morning’s Invocation**
The Dao is beyond naming—yet this very Heaven is called the Dao. Through fasting, reverence may be achieved. Pouring forth the sincerity of sunflowers turning to the sun, we beseech that the qi of fragrant herbs may move the divine. We pray for universal deliverance, benefiting both the living and the dead. As the departed flow like this river, may their *hun* return to Heaven, their *po* to Earth. For the living, may nurturance abound—blessings vast as the sea, longevity steadfast as mountains.

**Third Morning’s Invocation**
In serving the dead and the living, we fulfill the filial piety due to our honored parents. In revering the end as we revered the beginning, we uphold the solemnity of discipline. Our gratitude ascends to the Nine Heavens; our rites span three days. Completing the Nine Mornings’ Dao, we pray for the illumination of the Eight Luminaries, that our embodied selves may endure. May the names of the departed be inscribed early upon the Cinnabar Terrace’s stone chambers, and their souls find proof of refinement. Through the merit of the Golden Register and White Petitions, may all in darkness and light alike receive deliverance.

**Establishing the Morning Audience**
Heaven’s hearing is never distant; we ever hold our private sincerity in mind. Yet human affairs must end—how can we avoid repeated supplication? Overwhelmed and ashamed, we, the foolish and ignorant, reflect: fortunate to have attained human form, we are ever favored by the Emperor’s gaze, with abundance to our left and right. Knowing how to serve the dead and the living, we rely on the incense of cultivation to perfect this morning audience. We pray that the Eastern Realm of Eternal Joy and the Western Land of Na may both radiate light; that the Northern Springs’ Winding Palace and the Southern Palace of Shangchang may together achieve universal deliverance. May all sentient beings attain transcendence.

**Dispersing the Morning Audience**
The Heavenly Dao defies naming, yet it is wise and luminous. In the order of human relations, filial piety and reverence must come first. We prostrate ourselves, pouring forth our sorrow, lifting our voices to the azure vault. We reflect: dwelling in the Central Land, we share this private devotion. Through the purity of our fast, we fulfill the Way of honoring parents, mindful that though we were nurtured in life, we failed to fully repay their warmth.
